\doxysubsection*{\+\_\+}
\label{_amgrpb14a7b8059d9c055954c92674ce60032}%
Creates a {\ttfamily lodash} object which wraps {\ttfamily value} to enable implicit method chain sequences.

Methods that operate on and return arrays, collections, and functions can be chained together. Methods that retrieve a single value or may return a primitive value will automatically end the chain sequence and return the unwrapped value. Otherwise, the value must be unwrapped with {\ttfamily \+\_\+\#value}.

Explicit chain sequences, which must be unwrapped with {\ttfamily \+\_\+\#value}, may be enabled using {\ttfamily \+\_\+.\+chain}.

The execution of chained methods is lazy, that is, it\textquotesingle{}s deferred until {\ttfamily \+\_\+\#value} is implicitly or explicitly called.

Lazy evaluation allows several methods to support shortcut fusion. Shortcut fusion is an optimization to merge iteratee calls; this avoids the creation of intermediate arrays and can greatly reduce the number of iteratee executions. Sections of a chain sequence qualify for shortcut fusion if the section is applied to an array and iteratees accept only one argument. The heuristic for whether a section qualifies for shortcut fusion is subject to change.

Chaining is supported in custom builds as long as the {\ttfamily \+\_\+\#value} method is directly or indirectly included in the build.

In addition to lodash methods, wrappers have {\ttfamily Array} and {\ttfamily String} methods.

The wrapper {\ttfamily Array} methods are\+: {\ttfamily concat}, {\ttfamily join}, {\ttfamily pop}, {\ttfamily push}, {\ttfamily shift}, {\ttfamily sort}, {\ttfamily splice}, and {\ttfamily unshift}

The wrapper {\ttfamily String} methods are\+: {\ttfamily replace} and {\ttfamily split}

The wrapper methods that support shortcut fusion are\+: {\ttfamily at}, {\ttfamily compact}, {\ttfamily drop}, {\ttfamily drop\+Right}, {\ttfamily drop\+While}, {\ttfamily filter}, {\ttfamily find}, {\ttfamily find\+Last}, {\ttfamily head}, {\ttfamily initial}, {\ttfamily last}, {\ttfamily map}, {\ttfamily reject}, {\ttfamily reverse}, {\ttfamily slice}, {\ttfamily tail}, {\ttfamily take}, {\ttfamily take\+Right}, {\ttfamily take\+Right\+While}, {\ttfamily take\+While}, and {\ttfamily to\+Array}

The chainable wrapper methods are\+: {\ttfamily after}, {\ttfamily ary}, {\ttfamily assign}, {\ttfamily assign\+In}, {\ttfamily assign\+In\+With}, {\ttfamily assign\+With}, {\ttfamily at}, {\ttfamily before}, {\ttfamily bind}, {\ttfamily bind\+All}, {\ttfamily bind\+Key}, {\ttfamily cast\+Array}, {\ttfamily chain}, {\ttfamily chunk}, {\ttfamily commit}, {\ttfamily compact}, {\ttfamily concat}, {\ttfamily conforms}, {\ttfamily constant}, {\ttfamily count\+By}, {\ttfamily create}, {\ttfamily curry}, {\ttfamily debounce}, {\ttfamily defaults}, {\ttfamily defaults\+Deep}, {\ttfamily defer}, The base implementation of {\ttfamily base\+For\+Own} which iterates over {\ttfamily object} properties returned by {\ttfamily keys\+Func} and invokes {\ttfamily iteratee} for each property. 

Iteratee functions may exit iteration early by explicitly returning {\ttfamily false}.
